  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cbe4655e-ccf3-47b9-9749-a9e084c06dbb'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1693453412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1693453412" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1693453412?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=spirituality-philosophy">spirituality-philosophy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1693453412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6559036638195353683"><i>"Our lot as men is to learn and one goes to knowledge as one goes to war; I have told you this countless times. One goes to knowledge or to war with fear, with respect, aware that one is going to war, and with absolute confidence in oneself."<br/><br/>"In order to become a man of knowledge one must be a warrior, not a whimpering child. One must strive without giving up, without a complaint, without flinching, until one sees, only to realize then that nothing matters."</i><br/><br/>In this book, Castaneda returns to his</span>
  <span id="freeText6559036638195353683" style="display:none"><i>"Our lot as men is to learn and one goes to knowledge as one goes to war; I have told you this countless times. One goes to knowledge or to war with fear, with respect, aware that one is going to war, and with absolute confidence in oneself."<br /><br />"In order to become a man of knowledge one must be a warrior, not a whimpering child. One must strive without giving up, without a complaint, without flinching, until one sees, only to realize then that nothing matters."</i><br /><br />In this book, Castaneda returns to his apprenticeship with don Juan after leaving due to his fears after using don Juan‚Äôs ally (smoking mushrooms). There were a lot of rather dry descriptions of his visions - what the water looked like, lights, and other visuals. I missed the more philosophical and spiritual teachings from the first book.<br /><br />This one focused mainly on ‚Äúseeing‚Äù and learning to be a ‚Äúwarrior‚Äù and also more about sorcerers and allies. Allies ‚Äì I‚Äôm not quite clear on it, but I think they appear to be men/women that manifest after ingesting hallucinogens and can help people perform sorcery and act as guides? <br /><br />One of the most interesting ideas in this book is about how we shape our world/reality with our thoughts. Through our internal dialogue mainly, we tell ourselves such-and-such is true and so it is. We focus on <i>what people do</i> and it essentially <i>becomes a shield</i> that hides true reality, which is basically that the world is an endless mystery. We insist on <i>understanding</i> instead of opening ourselves up to the unknown. <br /><br />Instead of <i>seeing</i> with our spiritual eyes, we are trapped into a way of viewing things based on what our physical eyes are trained to <i>know</i>. <b>Seeing</b> instead of knowing is a huge theme in this second book.<br /><br />A lot of what don Juan said was cryptic. Castaneda spends a lot of time ‚Äúlistening‚Äù and performing ritualistic shamanistic acts which don‚Äôt seem to produce any major results (hand positions, which direction to sit in, wandering the mountains searching for a spirit catcher, etc.). You can see he is training and learning, but it doesn‚Äôt make for very exciting reading. <br /><br />There was a large section devoted to Castaneda and don Juan calling a spirit of the water. The spirit apparently liked Castaneda but he needed don Juan‚Äôs help to come back because the spirits can draw people to their deaths or a person will wander and never come back. <br /><br />I guess in the end, I wanted more interactions with the beings in the nonphysical world and less about the green mist, weird noises, and bubbles. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1691257348?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">My review</a> on book one, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/78250.The_Teachings_of_Don_Juan_A_Yaqui_Way_of_Knowledge_" title="The Teachings of Don Juan A Yaqui Way of Knowledge  by Carlos Castaneda" rel="nofollow noopener">The Teachings of Don Juan: A Yaqui Way of Knowledge</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6559036638195353683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1663390-sherry-sethurner?shelf=mind-and-spirit">mind-and-spirit</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151596345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12129642157886255161">Castaneda books were very popular when I was an undergraduate, and when I first started teaching in the 1970s. I remember reading all three and being amused and confused. I suspect I was mostly interested in the author's descriptions of his experiences with peyote. Years have passed, and I revisited A Separate Reality after a friend's adult son passed away. I saw imagery and a quote from Castaneda in his artwork, and thought this might be a time to see what I could learn from the book. What a di</span>
  <span id="freeText12129642157886255161" style="display:none">Castaneda books were very popular when I was an undergraduate, and when I first started teaching in the 1970s. I remember reading all three and being amused and confused. I suspect I was mostly interested in the author's descriptions of his experiences with peyote. Years have passed, and I revisited A Separate Reality after a friend's adult son passed away. I saw imagery and a quote from Castaneda in his artwork, and thought this might be a time to see what I could learn from the book. What a difference all those years of living made in my interest and understanding! I was fascinated in the student and mentor's different ways of perceiving the world, and in the ongoing conversation they have about the differences between looking and really seeing, between an intellectual understanding of the world and and experiential understanding. This time I felt Don Juan had something to teach me, not just Carlos, about living life as fully aware as possible, with intention, and respect for death, that comes for each of us.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12129642157886255161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2079040963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2079040963" />
    <a title="Syl Sabastian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48422533-syl-sabastian"><img alt="Syl Sabastian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520059100p2/48422533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2079040963?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Syl Sabastian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Syl Sabastian" href="/user/show/48422533-syl-sabastian">Syl Sabastian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2079040963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14538280155112267066">We read and we read, and then, we encounter, well, A Separate Reality. Much depends on how we read. If we're too immersed in story, we miss the More, if we're to concerned with artificial criteria of evaluation, we miss the Value, if we're too bubbled in our cocoon-of-self we miss the Usefulness. Within the distinct realism of A Separate Reality we find an overwhelm of potency, which, if we're not prepared to actually change our world, will pass us by.<br/><br/>To read this powerful and transformative wor</span>
  <span id="freeText14538280155112267066" style="display:none">We read and we read, and then, we encounter, well, A Separate Reality. Much depends on how we read. If we're too immersed in story, we miss the More, if we're to concerned with artificial criteria of evaluation, we miss the Value, if we're too bubbled in our cocoon-of-self we miss the Usefulness. Within the distinct realism of A Separate Reality we find an overwhelm of potency, which, if we're not prepared to actually change our world, will pass us by.<br /><br />To read this powerful and transformative work we have to DO much. Such as set aside our habits, including the habit of reading. Here we're required to stop, absorb, hear, imbibe, incorporate, assimilate, Apply, integrate, and actually Change. Not only who we are, but our entire conception of ourselves and which world we live in. We have to set aside our continuity, a difficult challenge for many, unhook from our conformity, our cosiness and indulgences. Discarding our habits-of-perception and our assumptions of focus is another. We have to perceive past the obvious and pay close Attention to that which requires no faith or belief, no external agents to implement, and in these pages we can find such power. There's much to gain if we make that effort to determine Value, Usefulness and Applicability for ourselves, with an open being.<br /><br />Too many get lost in the indulgence of connecting to the drug-story lure, which is immaterial to the magic of this book. Or they unnecessarily sideline themselves by needlessly debating whether Don Juan is real or not. What does it matter where a self-evident Value comes from? If you need someone to be real to determine whether an utterance or communication has Value or validity, well, then you're lost before you begin. Only you have that particular power, since you and you alone, are the Final-Arbiter-of-Truth. When we discern the wisdom and conceptualising genius so abundant in A Separate Reality we encounter a treasure trove of Life-Change.<br /><br />The inordinate Gift of A Separate reality is exactly that, a separate Reality-of-Being. Such a potential is gifted us in this monumental work if we can see past the tests-of-self which are part of this challenge-of-being. We have to look at the real power, which is the presentation of new conceptions of what it means to BE. Ways-of-Being which are distinct, new, foreign, even alien, yet attainable. Simple but complex, such as relinquishing the seduction of self-importance. We are not merely informed this may be valuable, the usefulness of this life-transformation is amply demonstrated for us by that marvellous example of Impeccability, Don Juan. <br /><br />I feel many make the mistake of identifying with the fool Carlos, because yes, of course we too are similar nincompoops, but, the real Gift I believe lies in stretching ourselves to identify with the *possibility* of being as much like Don Juan as we can. Once we grasp this as an actual potential actuality, we begin a Path where his Way-of-Being becomes our model, or standard, our code, our sensibility, and default measure for our Impeccability. If we simply ask ourselves how Don Juan would behave in whatever circumstance we find ourselves in, we have a fantastic self-leverage which is powerful and transformative. If we connect to Don Juan not for his magical powers, but to his essential Character-of-Self, we connect to his ethics, his integrity, his Joy-of-Being and all the other marvellous examples of a self we can move toward being. If we read this book in this way, well, it becomes much more than reading. Such is the nature of this mind-bloom.<br /><br />But, to connect to this power of the book, we have to read past the story, past the character interactions, and truly listen, truly hear what's conveyed. Our read-perception has to include identifying what we *don't* want, what's irrelevant and immaterial, and in that simple selectivity, we come to see what's truly of issue and important to our Deep-Self. We are thus required to read and connect to the implications of what's imparted, to look past the tests-of-self such as the rituals and the indulgences of Carlos and look at the Way-of-Living and Deep Sobriety Don Juan Shares so incredibly. Doing so connects us to what he's really offering, which is of course, a Gift of Power. <br /><br />Of all the thousands of books I've read, which include a substantial selection of classics from around the world, this incredible book stands out, and is a definite must-read and multiple-read. (Along with its extension, A Journey to Ixtlan.) To be sure, one can find all the conceptions and ideas elsewhere, however, not so compacted and cohesive, not presented as an example in practice, and also not in the excellent resonating language of Don Juan. When we read to hear him, feel him, know him, imbibe him, and connect to this paragon of possibility who is Don Juan, especially if we don't over-mythologise him, and read not to remember what he said, but to BE what he Shares, then we shift into our journey toward living in a reality which more and more becomes A Magic Reality of actuality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14538280155112267066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174524400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15144726470797051697">I recommend Carlos Castaneda's body of work, which had a great impact on my worldview. A Separate Reality (the second in the series) describes his studies with Don Juan, the Yaqui shaman that he first wrote about in Teachings of Don Juan, a Yaqui Way of Knowledge. Like Teachings, A Separate Reality explores the multiple realities that we experience in our lives, such as our dreams, which while we're dreaming are our true universe, and our waking reality, in which our dreams are just a fantasy. A</span>
  <span id="freeText15144726470797051697" style="display:none">I recommend Carlos Castaneda's body of work, which had a great impact on my worldview. A Separate Reality (the second in the series) describes his studies with Don Juan, the Yaqui shaman that he first wrote about in Teachings of Don Juan, a Yaqui Way of Knowledge. Like Teachings, A Separate Reality explores the multiple realities that we experience in our lives, such as our dreams, which while we're dreaming are our true universe, and our waking reality, in which our dreams are just a fantasy. A key concept in A Separate Reality is the difference between looking (which is what we do most of the time) and seeing (in which we perceive the essence of something). It is truly a mind-expanding book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15144726470797051697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3075901" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/166376-david">David</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3075901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3600679958339573327">When I was an undergraduate in the mid-70's, Castaneda's "Don Juan" trilogy (with maybe a little Hermann Hesse thrown in) was what one read to be considered deep and interesting. Thirty years on, Hesse still holds up (for the most part). For Castaneda one can only ask "What was I thinking?". <br/><br/>But presumably that's what undergraduate time should be used for - to read broadly and indiscriminately. So not everything you read in college is going to be good.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_524198560" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/524198560" />
    <a title="Diana Silaghi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1988589-diana-silaghi"><img alt="Diana Silaghi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/524198560?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana Silaghi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana Silaghi" href="/user/show/1988589-diana-silaghi">Diana Silaghi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer524198560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16656751671444907313">Don Juan had once told me that a man of knowledge had predilections. I asked him to explain his statement.<br/>"My predilection is to see," he said.<br/>"What do you mean by that?"<br/>"I like to see" he said, "because only by seeing can a man of knowledge know."<br/>"What kind of things do you see?"<br/>"Everything."<br/>"But I also see everything and I'm not a man of knowledge."<br/>"No. You don't see.<br/>"I think I do."<br/>"I tell you, you don't."<br/>"What makes you say that, don Juan?"<br/>"You only look at the surface of things."<br/>"Do you mean</span>
  <span id="freeText16656751671444907313" style="display:none">Don Juan had once told me that a man of knowledge had predilections. I asked him to explain his statement.<br />"My predilection is to see," he said.<br />"What do you mean by that?"<br />"I like to see" he said, "because only by seeing can a man of knowledge know."<br />"What kind of things do you see?"<br />"Everything."<br />"But I also see everything and I'm not a man of knowledge."<br />"No. You don't see.<br />"I think I do."<br />"I tell you, you don't."<br />"What makes you say that, don Juan?"<br />"You only look at the surface of things."<br />"Do you mean that every man of knowledge actually sees through everything he looks at?"<br />"No. That's not what I mean. I said that a man of knowledge has his own predilections; mine is just to see and<br />to know; others do other things."<br />"What other things, for example?"<br />"Take Sacateca, he's a man of knowledge and his predilection is dancing. So he dances and knows."<br />"Is the predilection of a man of knowledge something he does in order to know?"<br />"Yes, that is correct."<br />"But how could dancing help Sacateca to know?"<br />"One can say that Sacateca dances with all he has."<br />----------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br />"What's it like to see, don Juan?"<br />"You have to learn to see in order to know that. I can't tell you."<br />"Is it a secret I shouldn't know?"<br />"No. It's just that I can't describe it."<br />"Why?"<br />"It wouldn't make sense to you."<br />"Try me, don Juan. Maybe it'll make sense to me."<br />"No. You must do it yourself. Once you learn, you can see every single thing in the world in a different way."<br />"Then, don Juan, you don't see the world in the usual way any more."<br />"I see both ways. When I want to look at the world I see it the way you do. Then when I want to see it I look<br />at it the way I know and I perceive it in a different way."<br />"Do things look consistently the same every time you see them?"<br />"Things don't change. You change your way of looking, that's all"<br />"I mean, don Juan, that if you see, for instance, the same tree, does it remain the same every time you see it?"<br />"No. It changes and yet it's the same."<br />"But if the same tree changes every time you see it, your seeing may be a mere illusion."<br />He laughed and did not answer for some time, but seemed to be thinking. Finally he said, "Whenever you<br />look at things you don't see them. You just look at them, I suppose, to make sure that something is there. Since<br />you're not concerned with seeing, things look very much the same every time you look at them. When you learn<br />to see, on the other hand, a thing is never the same every time you see it, and yet it is the same. I told you, for instance, that a man is like an egg. Every time I see the same man I see an egg, yet it is not the same egg."<br />"But you won't be able to recognize anything, since nothing is the same; so what's the advantage of learning<br />to see?"<br />"You can tell things apart. You can see them for what they really are."<br />------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br />twisted book...</span>

The three were eventually issued as a cloth trilogy. I started the series in paperback, but found the trilogy soon after and purchased it, probably at Stuart Brent Bookstore in Chicago near where I worked during the summer months between college and seminary.</span>

<div id="review_483329927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/483329927" />
    <a title="Rob Poole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15705937-rob-poole"><img alt="Rob Poole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356276217p2/15705937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/483329927?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob Poole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob Poole" href="/user/show/15705937-rob-poole">Rob Poole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15705937-rob-poole?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15705937-rob-poole?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15705937-rob-poole?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer483329927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5080833966383282176">There is another world just beyond our reach and we only need to seek it to find it.<br/><br/>In the 1960s Carlos Castaneda made his way to Mexico to learn more about Yaqui Indians and to do a little soul searching. What he found was a man named don Juan, a very powerful sorcerer and a force to be reckoned with. Don Juan turns Castaneda's whole world upside down by teaching him the ways of a sorcerer and the results are some of the most beautiful and touching pieces of nonfiction.<br/><br/>In "A Separate Reality" C</span>
  <span id="freeText5080833966383282176" style="display:none">There is another world just beyond our reach and we only need to seek it to find it.<br /><br />In the 1960s Carlos Castaneda made his way to Mexico to learn more about Yaqui Indians and to do a little soul searching. What he found was a man named don Juan, a very powerful sorcerer and a force to be reckoned with. Don Juan turns Castaneda's whole world upside down by teaching him the ways of a sorcerer and the results are some of the most beautiful and touching pieces of nonfiction.<br /><br />In "A Separate Reality" Castaneda attempts to explain don Juan's teachings about the art of 'seeing'. Through the use of a hallucinogenic substance of don Juan's own creation Castaneda experiences visions that shake him to his very core. <br /><br />Don Juan also explains the importance of becoming a warrior. A warrior is someone who is ever ready to perform to the best of their ability by being aware of every opportunity and using it to their advantage. According to don Juan it is inherent that one become a warrior before becoming a sorcerer.<br /><br />Often Castaneda finds himself in over his head. He rushes into this new world with a childlike wonder that is refreshing and a curiosity that is commendable. However, his curiosity seems insatiable. There is no end to his quest to understand the world of don Juan's sorcery, and this leads him to question don Juan's teachings until they are imperceptible. Every new experience brings innumerable questions from Castaneda's brain and many of them are unanswerable. Don Juan seems to do his absolute best to explain and some of his explanations are truly beautiful, but at times it seems like Castaneda is missing the point.<br /><br />Throughout "A Separate Reality" I found myself questioning my own views of the world. Don Juan has a way of making you think twice about nearly everything you've come to accept and Castaneda describes his experiences with a deftness the likes of which I have rarely seen. <br /><br />I enjoy Carlos Castaneda's work. His quiet prose and humble outlook ring true in my heart. I feel for Carlos in every situation that don Juan puts him through. I understand his fear and confusion almost inherently. There were moments in "A Separate Reality" where I found myself laughing out loud, Castaneda's experiences with don Juan's friend don Genaro are especially hilarious. There were moments where I found myself gripped with fear, such as Castaneda's first experience with an 'ally.' Castaneda has an incredible ability to pour his heart on to every page.<br /><br />My overall impression of "A Separate Reality" has left me wanting more. The intriguing world of don Juan has inspired me. To paraphrase don Juan, once you are introduced to his world there is no turning back as you realize there is no other way to live.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5080833966383282176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1505908724" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1505908724" />
    <a title="Leo Walsh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2118933-leo-walsh"><img alt="Leo Walsh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442889406p2/2118933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1505908724?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leo Walsh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leo Walsh" href="/user/show/2118933-leo-walsh">Leo Walsh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1505908724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13838018509382501214">Second Don Juan book. A little weaker than the first. Plus, there are hints of Hindu and Buddhist philosophy re-packaged as native American wisdom. Old wine in new [age] skins... <br/><br/>But instead of reading these as the non-fiction they are marketed as, I am reading them as fantasies. <br/><br/>That said, I love the new character Castaneda introduces here, don Genaro. A true trickster, he makes me laugh. But the "wisdom" revealed here is less interesting than the "wisdom" revealed in the first volume. Instead </span>
  <span id="freeText13838018509382501214" style="display:none">Second Don Juan book. A little weaker than the first. Plus, there are hints of Hindu and Buddhist philosophy re-packaged as native American wisdom. Old wine in new [age] skins... <br /><br />But instead of reading these as the non-fiction they are marketed as, I am reading them as fantasies. <br /><br />That said, I love the new character Castaneda introduces here, don Genaro. A true trickster, he makes me laugh. But the "wisdom" revealed here is less interesting than the "wisdom" revealed in the first volume. Instead of grounded, here Castaneda seems to imply that the etheric body has physical manifestations. <br /><br />It may or it may not. But as most true spiritual masters have pointed out -- Jesus, Buddha, etc. -- grasping for power gets you stuck. So perceiving and using your etheric body to gain power over the spiritual realm is a trap.<br /><br />That said, I do not know how to rate these books. As fantasies, they are okay, ranking as a lesser Ursula K. Le Guin. What's more, the "wisdom," is often pretty good, and more grounded than the "think and grow rich" nonsense that New Age has developed into, like "The Secret." <br /><br />The problem is that today, most (if not all) archaeologists who look at Castenada's work in depth think he made "Don Juan" up. There are many tip-offs, but the most notable are his naming of plants and animals. Instead of Amerindian names, he gives them common American and Spanish names. <br /><br />And Castenada died defending (if not believing) his own guff. I can understand Castaneda's delusions. He was, from all appearances, a seeker who created a powerful "imaginary friend" who was an ally in his maturation. He fell prey to one of the seven deadly sins -- pride. He had used don Juan to get his PhD at UCLA. To state the truth would have made him admit he was a fraud. So he hunkered down, and his pride made him believe his fiction.<br /><br />So while I understand, though do not excuse, Castenada, I cannot understand the publisher. By now, they know that Castaneda's field work was fraudulent. And yet the market it as non-fiction. So I can only give the book two stars.<br /><br />For my full explanation of my feelings on Castaneda, please read my review of <a href="" rel="nofollow noopener">"The teachings of Don Juan: A Yaqui Way of Knowledge."</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13838018509382501214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_131636880" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131636880" />
    <a title="Aaron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/231773-aaron"><img alt="Aaron" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131636880?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron" href="/user/show/231773-aaron">Aaron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131636880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2289695341132295919">This book would probably seem strange to most and only interesting to a few. For me I can only say that this book chose me, it came to me at a time in my life in which I was approaching a major spiritual awakening, though I didn't know it. This book helped push me over the edge. I feel if I would have read it any time sooner than when I did it would have been lost on me. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6235415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9463707103493017925">I am going to give the same review to all the Carlos Castaneda books I read in that series, simply because they are all outstanding. I was lucky to come across Castaneda very early on my magickal path. My spells and rituals have always relied on the power of intent, and I have found no better education on how to focus your intent than in this series of books. Back then (1994) they were classifed as nonfiction. Lately, they say they are fiction. All I know is much of what is in these books works.</span>
  <span id="freeText9463707103493017925" style="display:none">I am going to give the same review to all the Carlos Castaneda books I read in that series, simply because they are all outstanding. I was lucky to come across Castaneda very early on my magickal path. My spells and rituals have always relied on the power of intent, and I have found no better education on how to focus your intent than in this series of books. Back then (1994) they were classifed as nonfiction. Lately, they say they are fiction. All I know is much of what is in these books works. And having been a Wiccan Faery Witch now for 13 years I know much of what is real to us is fiction to those not walking a magickal path. These are life-changing books you will never forget, and their teachings still influence my life today. Can't get any better than that!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2196260960" />
    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62688146-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482165019p2/62688146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2196260960?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/62688146-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62688146-catherine?shelf=spirituality">spirituality</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196260960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3699821029221111891">Read this mostly in one sitting at the DMV. A world-altering read for me. The book starts slow but careens into mystical extremes by the second half. Castaneda plays the role of the modern person: rational, verbal, objective. Castaneda is amazingly, remarkably bad at succumbing to metaphysical experience. This is hilarious and endearing. Castaneda might have been resisting the non-linear because he was ostensibly doing anthropological research. In any case this makes Castaneda a relatable foil t</span>
  <span id="freeText3699821029221111891" style="display:none">Read this mostly in one sitting at the DMV. A world-altering read for me. The book starts slow but careens into mystical extremes by the second half. Castaneda plays the role of the modern person: rational, verbal, objective. Castaneda is amazingly, remarkably bad at succumbing to metaphysical experience. This is hilarious and endearing. Castaneda might have been resisting the non-linear because he was ostensibly doing anthropological research. In any case this makes Castaneda a relatable foil to the winking Don Juan.<br /><br />The format of the book, a series of conversations between teacher and student, is poetic. It would make a beautiful novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3699821029221111891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_938461114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/938461114" />
    <a title="Iona  Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5485612-iona-stewart"><img alt="Iona  Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311366951p2/5485612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/938461114?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iona  Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iona  Stewart" href="/user/show/5485612-iona-stewart">Iona  Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer938461114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6787689443462369996">I read a biography (The life and teachings of Carlos Castaneda) of Castaneda previously and was rather put off about him, since it turned out he was by no means a pleasant character. I thus did not plan to read any more of his books. But then I found this one and thought I would try it.<br/><br/>I didn‚Äôt find it as good as some of the other books. Don Juan, the Yaqui Indian who was training Carlos to be a sorcerer, or whatever, kept getting him to do such strange, complicated, and, according to what Don J</span>
  <span id="freeText6787689443462369996" style="display:none">I read a biography (The life and teachings of Carlos Castaneda) of Castaneda previously and was rather put off about him, since it turned out he was by no means a pleasant character. I thus did not plan to read any more of his books. But then I found this one and thought I would try it.<br /><br />I didn‚Äôt find it as good as some of the other books. Don Juan, the Yaqui Indian who was training Carlos to be a sorcerer, or whatever, kept getting him to do such strange, complicated, and, according to what Don Juan said, deadly dangerous, things that it was difficult to find rhyme or reason in them.<br /><br />And Carlos did not seem to get anything out of it at all.<br /><br />Previously, Carlos was wanting information about plants, especially peyote, which is a hallucinogenic cactus.<br /><br />Carlos was a student of anthropology interested in medicinal plants but was also extremely curious about Don Juan. His eyes shone ‚Äúwith a light of their own‚Äù.<br /><br />They became friends. But Carlos was interested in ‚Äúacademic knowledge that transcends experience‚Äù whereas Don Juan talked about direct knowledge of the world.<br /><br />Don Juan tells Carlos he must ‚Äúfeel everything, otherwise the world loses its sense‚Äù.<br /><br />Don Juan tells him that Carlos shuts off the world around him and clings to his arguments: therefore all he has are problems.<br /><br />Don Juan calls peyote ‚ÄúMescalito‚Äù and said Mescalito taught ‚Äúthe right way of life‚Äù, He regarded jimson weed and the mushrooms as powers of a different sort. He called them ‚Äúallies‚Äù and said a sorcerer ‚Äúdrew his strength from manipulating an ally‚Äù. The power contained in the mushroom was Don Juan‚Äôs personal ally, and he called it ‚Äúsmoke‚Äù or ‚Äúlittle smoke‚Äù.<br /><br />Carlos began to lose the certainty that ‚Äúthe reality of everyday life is something we can take for granted‚Äù.<br /><br />Don Juan‚Äôs premise was that a light, amenable disposition was needed in order to understand the impact and strangeness of the knowledge he was teaching Carlos.<br /><br />‚ÄúTo be a man of knowledge one needs to be light and fluid.‚Äù<br /><br />Don Juan tried to teach Carlos to ‚Äúsee‚Äù. ‚ÄúLooking‚Äù was the ordinary way of perceiving the world, while ‚Äúseeing‚Äù entailed a complex process by which a man of knowledge perceives the ‚Äúessence‚Äù of the things of the world.<br /><br />Smoking the mixture was indispensable for ‚Äúseeing‚Äù.<br /><br />Part One of the book is called ‚ÄúThe Preliminaries of Seeing‚Äù and Part Two ‚ÄúThe Task of Seeing‚Äù.<br /><br />Don Juan tells Carlos that ‚Äúthe little smoke‚Äù will help him to ‚Äúsee‚Äù men as fibres of light.<br /><br />Don Juan had a sense of drama, and humour.<br /><br />Many things Don Juan says seem cryptic. Carlos keeps asking him to explain what he means. Don Juan tells about ‚Äúcontrolled folly‚Äù.<br /><br />Nothing one does is important. ‚ÄúControlled folly‚Äù is very much like ‚Äúseeing‚Äù; it is something you cannot think about.<br /><br />In order to become a man of knowledge one must be a warrior. ‚ÄúOne must strive without giving up --- until one ‚Äúsees‚Äù., only to realize then that nothing matters.‚Äù<br /><br />He records everything that occurs in great detail, including the exact dates on which they occur. He describes everything accurately, pedantically.<br /><br />I found the book absolutely readable, though didn‚Äôt feel I really understood everything, perhaps nothing. Don Juan‚Äôs world was a different one from ours and his knowledge a different sort of knowledge.<br /><br />But if the world of sorcery. ‚Äúseeing‚Äù and becoming a man of knowledge interest you, then read the book. I‚Äôm not sure, but I think it was Castaneda‚Äôs second book. Happy reading!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6787689443462369996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_986635866" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/986635866" />
    <a title="Aaron Dennis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6813582-aaron-dennis"><img alt="Aaron Dennis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574179817p2/6813582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/986635866?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Dennis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Dennis" href="/user/show/6813582-aaron-dennis">Aaron Dennis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer986635866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8049419614235995109">A Separate Reality is the second book written by Carlos Castaneda, and while still practically mired in the realm of hallucinogenic mixtures, a few new topics are brought to life; seeing, living like a warrior, and shutting off the internal dialogue.<br/><br/>It is those three concepts, which bring a rather large change to the narrative presentation. Some people argue that it is because the book veers away from the initial inspections of the first book that it must all be fake. Okay, very possible. It is </span>
  <span id="freeText8049419614235995109" style="display:none">A Separate Reality is the second book written by Carlos Castaneda, and while still practically mired in the realm of hallucinogenic mixtures, a few new topics are brought to life; seeing, living like a warrior, and shutting off the internal dialogue.<br /><br />It is those three concepts, which bring a rather large change to the narrative presentation. Some people argue that it is because the book veers away from the initial inspections of the first book that it must all be fake. Okay, very possible. It is also possible, as Castaneda states later on, that his conglomeration of notes were mostly tossed aside because he believed the teachings were predicated on tripping balls.<br /><br />So, it isn‚Äôt that the story or characters have changed, it‚Äôs that Castaneda uses previously unused notes in his story.<br /><br />I want to stop here and state firmly that I am not trying to convince anyone that we can be sorcerers. It‚Äôs simply that these stories have had an overwhelming impact on my life and I see how stale everyone else around me is, yet I see the world as something new and fresh everyday‚Ä¶<br /><br />Anyway, if nothing else, the story if used as an allegory can still show us what many books, T.V. programs, movies, etc., show us- ways to enrich our lives. The actual events don‚Äôt have to be true or accurate. The bible may well not be real, but the teachings are still valid, no? Once more, I‚Äôm not saying the bible is fake, but it is written by God‚Äôs fallible man. The only thing God ever wrote was the 10 commandments, and if you look into the real commandments, not the ones altered in the 19th century, they are very powerful and actually fit quite well with Don Juan‚Äôs living as a warrior.<br /><br />So here‚Äôs a little exchange from A Separate Reality that I really enjoy:<br /><br />Juan looked at me with an air of disbelief then broke into laughter.<br /><br />‚ÄúWhat would you do?‚Äù I urged him.<br /><br />‚ÄúIf someone is waiting for me with a rifle with a telescopic sight?‚Äù he said, obviously mocking me.<br /><br />‚ÄúIf someone is hiding out of sight, waiting for you. You won‚Äôt have a chance. You can‚Äôt stop a bullet.‚Äù<br /><br />‚ÄúNo. I can‚Äôt, but I still don‚Äôt understand your point.‚Äù<br /><br />‚ÄúMy point is that all your strategy cannot be of any help in a situation like that.‚Äù<br /><br />‚ÄúOh, but it can. If someone is waiting for me with a powerful rifle with a telescopic sight I simply will not come around.‚Äù<br /><br />There you have it. This is key for martial artists too. The first line of defense is not be in the way of danger; to not be pinned down by routines. In essence, this is living as a warrior.<br /><br />As a whole, the book is nearly perfect; funny and lighthearted at times, filled with anticipation at others, it paints beautiful pictures, and will take you to another world‚Ä¶even if it is only in your mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8049419614235995109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2503371631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14963390725867082715">I like this more sober approach to spiritual reality. It is an individual journey and there are benefits and dangers at every turn. Compared to the generic assertions of some new age spirituality, referring to abstractions such as the absolute and how we are all interconnected, etc... They feel like intellectualisations of something that can't be intellectualised and they make it seem that ultimate reality is quite a simplistic, passive thing to understand. This book only really hints at some as</span>
  <span id="freeText14963390725867082715" style="display:none">I like this more sober approach to spiritual reality. It is an individual journey and there are benefits and dangers at every turn. Compared to the generic assertions of some new age spirituality, referring to abstractions such as the absolute and how we are all interconnected, etc... They feel like intellectualisations of something that can't be intellectualised and they make it seem that ultimate reality is quite a simplistic, passive thing to understand. This book only really hints at some aspects of the shamanism approach, such as controlled folly, and the use of certain hallucinatory drugs in order to speed up your ability to perceive these higher frequencies of reality where you can encounter things such as your ally. But you can easily get some of the theory and principles of shamanism from other sources. This gives you a story of one persons voyage of initiation into this way of life, where even when you remain incredulous of the details of some of the claims about what is happening you can appreciate the human journey being undertaken.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14963390725867082715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2732583339486874735">Can't get enough of what Don Juan has to say. After reading the first 3 books, I am of the opinion that - While people believe Don juan is a figment of Castaneda's imagination, I feel it's the other the other way round (in a philosophical way). Castaneda is all of us, with his skepticism and awkwardness. Don Juan is the true protagonist and Castaneda is a messenger Don Juan uses to invoke a curiosity in all the readers of the books about a separate reality. It's no coincidence, it's a deliberate</span>
  <span id="freeText2732583339486874735" style="display:none">Can't get enough of what Don Juan has to say. After reading the first 3 books, I am of the opinion that - While people believe Don juan is a figment of Castaneda's imagination, I feel it's the other the other way round (in a philosophical way). Castaneda is all of us, with his skepticism and awkwardness. Don Juan is the true protagonist and Castaneda is a messenger Don Juan uses to invoke a curiosity in all the readers of the books about a separate reality. It's no coincidence, it's a deliberate move. There are too many parallels of Don Juan's teachings with those in books like Autobiography of a Yogi or even Many Lives Many Masters. He is definitely one of those masters.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h5K/xMhYnaaS+Tl/65X6z5H6uKUyO3S315aFRRaYFdlCqEcKHy+lAzEYTM3FzOC4iz7Exkhvi1xup7Cui9PHMw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('60XUIB22YrXV4enaYUN3WJj5dtg8mSz/xxMmLyEezgEufyzuysFaEHYAnGhPGm0vgj0Ku0bN0xR+IhPEvFUc6w==')})
  }

It has exerted a living influence in China for 3000 years and interest in it has spread in the West. \n\nSet down in the dawn of history as a book of oracles, the Book of Changes deepened in meaning when ethical values were attached to the oracular pronouncements; it became a book of wisdom, eventually one of the Five Classics of Confucianism, and provided the common source for both Confucianist and Taoist philosophy. \n\nWilhelm\'s rendering of the I Ching into German, published in 1924, presented it for the 1st time in a form intelligible to the general reader. Wilhelm, who translated many other ancient Chinese works and who wrote several books on Chinese philosophy and civilization, long resided in China. His close association with its cultural leaders gave him a unique understanding of the text of the I Ching. In the English translation, every effort has been made to preserve Wilhelm\'s pioneering insight into the spirit of the original.\n\nThis 3rd edition, completely reset, contains a new forward by Hellmut Wilhelm, one of the most eminent American scholars of Chinese culture. He discusses his father\'s textual methods and summarizes recent studies of the I Ching both in the West and in present-day China. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10059082390242722383">Carlos Castaneda was an American author.<br/>Starting with The Teachings of Don Juan in 1968, Castaneda wrote a series of books that describe his training in shamanism, particularly with a group whose lineage descended from the Toltecs. <br/>The books, narrated in the first person, relate his experiences under the tutelage of a man that Castaneda claimed was a Yaqui "Man of Knowledge" named don Juan Matus. </span>
  <span id="freeText10059082390242722383" style="display:none">Carlos Castaneda was an American author.<br />Starting with The Teachings of Don Juan in 1968, Castaneda wrote a series of books that describe his training in shamanism, particularly with a group whose lineage descended from the Toltecs. <br />The books, narrated in the first person, relate his experiences under the tutelage of a man that Castaneda claimed was a Yaqui "Man of Knowledge" named don Juan Matus. His 12 books have sold more than 28 million copies in 17 languages. <br />Critics have suggested that they are works of fiction; supporters claim the books are either true or at least valuable works of philosophy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10059082390242722383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1430297-a-separate-reality">Quotes from A Separate Reality</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;We are men and our lot in life is to learn and to be hurled into inconceivable new worlds.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/58474-we-are-men-and-our-lot-in-life-is-to">64 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;To be a warrior a man has to be, first of all, and rightfully so, keenly aware of his own death. But to be concerned with death would force any one of us to focus on the self and that would be debilitating. So the next thing one needs to be a warrior is detachment. The idea of imminent death, instead of becoming an obsession, becomes an indifference.<br />Now you must detach yourself; detach yourself from everything. Only the idea of death makes a man sufficiently detached so he is incapable of abandoning himself to anything. Only the idea of death makes a man sufficiently detached so he can't deny himself anything. A man of that sort, however, does not crave, for he has acquired a silent lust for life and for all things of life. He knows his death is stalking him and won't give him time to cling to anything, so he tries, without craving, all of everything.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1344744-to-be-a-warrior-a-man-has-to-be-first">26 likes</a>
            </nobr>
